<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2007 Pacific typhoon season</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>The <b>2007 Pacific typhoon season</b> was a below average season which featured 24 named storms and 14 typhoons,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMAATCR_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMAATCR-1">[1]</a></sup> compared to the average of 27 and 17 respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CUHK_April_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-CUHK_April-2">[2]</a></sup> had no official bounds; it ran year-round in 2007, but most <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a> tend to form in the northwestern Pacific Ocean between May and November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP2003_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-GP2003-3">[3]</a></sup> These dates conventionally delimit the period of each year when most tropical cyclones form in the northwestern Pacific Ocean.</p>
<p>The scope of this article is limited to the Pacific Ocean, north of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a> and west of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_date_line" title="International date line">international date line</a>. Storms that form east of the date line and north of the equator are called hurricanes; see <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2007 Pacific hurricane season">2007 Pacific hurricane season</a>. Tropical Storms formed in the entire West Pacific basin are assigned a name by the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> (JMA). Tropical depressions in this basin have the "W" suffix added to their <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> identifier. In addition, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration</a> (PAGASA) assigns names to tropical cyclones (including tropical depressions) that enter or form in the Philippine area of responsibility. These names, however, are not in common use outside of the Philippines. This can also result in the same storm having two names.</p>
<p>According to PAGASA, the Philippines had its second quietest season with 14 named storms since the <a href="/wiki/1998_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="1998 Pacific typhoon season">1998 season</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/2010_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2010 Pacific typhoon season">2010</a> being the most quiet season.</p>
<p></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_University_of_Hong_Kong">City University of Hong Kong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: City University of Hong Kong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/2000_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2000 Pacific typhoon season">2000 typhoon season</a>, the Laboratory for Atmospheric Research (LAR), of the <a href="/wiki/City_University_of_Hong_Kong" title="City University of Hong Kong">City University of Hong Kong</a> have issued <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_seasonal_forecasting" title="Tropical cyclone seasonal forecasting">forecasts of activity</a> for each upcoming typhoon season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CUHK_April_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-CUHK_April-2">[2]</a></sup> Forecasts were released in April and June predicting how many tropical cyclones, tropical storms, and typhoons there will be during the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CUHK_April_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-CUHK_April-2">[2]</a></sup> During the season, the LAR is predicting a below average season with fewer than usual tropical cyclones. In its April forecast, the LAR predicted that 28 tropical cyclones, 25 tropical storms, and 14 typhoons before in its June forecast predicting 27 tropical cyclones, 24 tropical storms and 14 typhoons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CUHK_April_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-CUHK_April-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CUHK_June_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-CUHK_June-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Risk_Consortium">Tropical Storm Risk Consortium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Risk Consortium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the 2000 typhoon season, the Tropical Storm Risk Consortium (TSR) of the University College of London have issued forecasts of activity for each upcoming typhoon season. During 2007, forecasts were released in March, May, June, July and August predicting how many tropical cyclones, tropical storms, typhoons and intense typhoons there will be during a season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[nb 1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_March2_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_March2-12">[11]</a></sup> In its March forecast, TSR predicted that the season would be about 15% below average with 24 tropical storms, 15 typhoons and 7 intense typhoons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_March_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_March-4">[4]</a></sup> In its May forecast, TSR predicted that the season would now be near normal with 27 tropical storms, 17 typhoons and 8 intense typhoons forming during the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_May_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_May-5">[5]</a></sup> Within their June July and August forecasts, TSR forecasted the season would be near normal with 27 tropical storms and 17 typhoons forming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_June_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_June-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_July_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_July-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_August_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_August-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_meteorological_service_predictions">National meteorological service predictions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: National meteorological service predictions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration</a> (PAGASA), reported on January 27, 2007, that they were expecting 15–19 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone" title="Tropical Cyclone">tropical cyclones</a> to move through their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">area of responsibility</a>, during the upcoming typhoon season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAGJAN_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-PAGJAN-9">[9]</a></sup> They also predicted that due to the weak <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Niño">El Niño</a> event that was occurring the first tropical cyclone wouldn't move through their area of responsibility until May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAGJAN_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-PAGJAN-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2007_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="Timeline of the 2007 Pacific typhoon season">Timeline of the 2007 Pacific typhoon season</a></div>
<p>In storm information below, please note that on the following list, storms are listed by Tropical Depression number, and therefore Mitag (23W), which is on the naming list before Hagibis (24W), is listed after Hagibis, having been the later storm to form, despite being the earlier to attain Tropical Storm status. Please also note that wind-speed advisories differ from the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> (JTWC) to the JMA as the JTWC uses the United States criteria of 1-minute mean to designate maximum sustained winds, while the JMA uses the 10-minute mean wind criteria to designate tropical cyclone maximum sustained winds. This difference generally results in JTWC maximum winds appearing higher than the maximum winds described by the JMA for the same cyclone.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Kong-rey">Typhoon Kong-rey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Typhoon Kong-rey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kong-rey_03_apr_2007_0348Z.jpg"><img alt="Kong-rey 03 apr 2007 0348Z.jpg" data-file-height="9360" data-file-width="7681" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Kong-rey_03_apr_2007_0348Z.jpg/150px-Kong-rey_03_apr_2007_0348Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Kong-rey_03_apr_2007_0348Z.jpg/225px-Kong-rey_03_apr_2007_0348Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Kong-rey_03_apr_2007_0348Z.jpg/300px-Kong-rey_03_apr_2007_0348Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kong-rey_2007_track.png"><img alt="Kong-rey 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Kong-rey_2007_track.png/150px-Kong-rey_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Kong-rey_2007_track.png/225px-Kong-rey_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Kong-rey_2007_track.png/300px-Kong-rey_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>March 30 – April 6</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>150 km/h (90 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  960 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Kong-rey_(2007)" title="Typhoon Kong-rey (2007)">Typhoon Kong-rey (2007)</a></div>
<p>On March 26, the JTWC identified a broad area of low pressure in the Western North Pacific. It moved west-northwestward over the next few days, slowly gaining organization. According to the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a>, it became a tropical depression on March 30. The next day, the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> due to an increased consolidation of the low-level circulation of the system. The JTWC issued its first warning on Tropical Depression 01W late that evening local time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWCAdvisory1_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWCAdvisory1-13">[12]</a></sup> As it continued to strengthen, the JTWC upgraded it to a tropical storm,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWCadvisory2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWCadvisory2-14">[13]</a></sup> the first of the season. The JMA followed suit, and named the system Kong-rey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMA.27supgrade_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMA.27supgrade-15">[14]</a></sup> The name was submitted by Cambodia, and refers to a character in a <a href="/wiki/Khmer_people" title="Khmer people">Khmer</a> legend, which is also the name of a mountain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-names_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-names-16">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kong-rey continued to organize and intensified into a severe tropical storm early the next morning local time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMAupgradefromaTropicalStormtoaSevereTropicalStorm_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMAupgradefromaTropicalStormtoaSevereTropicalStorm-17">[16]</a></sup> The JTWC then upgraded it to a typhoon on April 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JointTyphoonWarningCenterwarning7_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-JointTyphoonWarningCenterwarning7-18">[17]</a></sup> As the system took a more poleward track towards the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">Northern Mariana Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service</a> office in <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> noted that damaging winds were now not expected on the island. Elsewhere in the Marianas, preparations were made and flights were cancelled in anticipation of the typhoon. Kong-rey passed through the islands in the early hours of the morning on April 3 local time. The JMA upgraded Kong-rey to a typhoon later that afternoon,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JmaAdvisoryupgradingSTSKong-reytoTyphoonKong-rey_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-JmaAdvisoryupgradingSTSKong-reytoTyphoonKong-rey-19">[18]</a></sup> as it developed an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a>. It strengthened slightly further before encountering <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> and colder <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperatures</a> and was downgraded back to a severe tropical storm on April 4. As Kong-rey accelerated towards the northeast, it began undergoing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extratropical_transition" title="Extratropical transition">extratropical transition</a> early on April 5 and the JTWC issued its final warning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JtwcfinaladvisoryonKong-rey_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-JtwcfinaladvisoryonKong-rey-20">[19]</a></sup> The JMA issued its final warning on the morning of April 6 after it had completed extratropical transition. No casualties or major damage was reported.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Yutu_.28Amang.29">Typhoon Yutu (Amang)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Typhoon Yutu (Amang)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 super typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TY_Yutu_2007_MODIS_May_20.jpg"><img alt="TY Yutu 2007 MODIS May 20.jpg" data-file-height="7022" data-file-width="6059" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/TY_Yutu_2007_MODIS_May_20.jpg/150px-TY_Yutu_2007_MODIS_May_20.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/TY_Yutu_2007_MODIS_May_20.jpg/225px-TY_Yutu_2007_MODIS_May_20.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/TY_Yutu_2007_MODIS_May_20.jpg/300px-TY_Yutu_2007_MODIS_May_20.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yutu_2007_track.png"><img alt="Yutu 2007 track.png" data-file-height="635" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Yutu_2007_track.png/150px-Yutu_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Yutu_2007_track.png/225px-Yutu_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Yutu_2007_track.png/300px-Yutu_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>May 17 – May 23</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>175 km/h (110 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  935 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On May 15, a significant consolidation of organisation in a tropical disturbance located south-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> led to <a href="/wiki/Dvorak_technique" title="Dvorak technique">Dvorak technique</a> numbers equating to a windspeed of 45 knots (83 km/h) from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_Force_Weather_Agency" title="Air Force Weather Agency">Air Force Weather Agency</a>. Later that day, the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> designated the system a tropical depression, and the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> The next day, the JMA began issuing full advisories on the tropical depression. It developed slowly, resulting in a reissuance of the TCFA later that day. In this second TCFA, the JTWC noted "an increasingly well-defined" low-level circulation centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> The JTWC upgraded the system to Tropical Depression 02W at 1200 UTC, based on satellite intensity estimates and <a href="/wiki/QuikSCAT" title="QuikSCAT">QuikSCAT</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The JMA designated 02W as Tropical Storm Yutu early on May 17, as the system strengthened further. The name 'Yutu' was contributed by China, and refers to a rabbit in a Chinese <a href="/wiki/Fable" title="Fable">fable</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-names_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-names-16">[15]</a></sup> The JTWC followed suit 3 hours later, upgrading the system to Tropical Storm 02W as it moved quickly westwards, heading for <a href="/wiki/Yap" title="Yap">Yap</a>. Tropical storm warnings and watches were put in place for most of the <a href="/wiki/Yap" title="Yap">Yap State</a>, but were later cancelled after Yutu passed through quickly.</p>
<p>It then took a northwesterly turn, entered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> area of responsibility on May 18 as it reached severe tropical storm strength,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> and was named "Amang". Later that day, the JTWC upgraded it to a typhoon, and identified a "distinct <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye feature</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> and the JMA upgraded the severe tropical storm to a typhoon at 1800 UTC as it continued to intensify. It began to recurve towards <a href="/wiki/Iwo_Jima" title="Iwo Jima">Iwo Jima</a>, undergoing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">rapid intensification</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> with "enhanced poleward outflow and low vertical <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> It reached its peak on the evening of May 20, as a strong <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 4-equivalent</a> typhoon, just short of becoming a super typhoon.</p>
<p>Despite moving into cooler waters, its strong poleward outflow helped it to maintain a high intensity, while carrying a 20 nautical mile-wide eye, on the early morning of May 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> It then began to gradually weaken, passing over <a href="/wiki/Okinotorishima" title="Okinotorishima">Okinotorishima</a> and near Iwo Jima that day as it sped off to the northeast. Maximum winds on Iwo Jima occurred around 1500 UTC that day, with 66 kt (122 km/h, 76 mph) sustained gusting to 104 kt (193 km/h, 120 mph), when a minimum central pressure of 976 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> was recorded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> It then started <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extratropical_transition" title="Extratropical transition">extratropical transition</a>, and the JTWC issued its final warning on the morning of May 22. The JMA issued its last advisory after extratropical transition completed a day later.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Toraji">Tropical Storm Toraji</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Toraji">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Toraji_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Toraji (2007)">Tropical Storm Toraji (2007)</a></div>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Toraji_20070704_NRL.jpg"><img alt="TS Toraji 20070704 NRL.jpg" data-file-height="3800" data-file-width="3800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/TS_Toraji_20070704_NRL.jpg/150px-TS_Toraji_20070704_NRL.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/TS_Toraji_20070704_NRL.jpg/225px-TS_Toraji_20070704_NRL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/TS_Toraji_20070704_NRL.jpg/300px-TS_Toraji_20070704_NRL.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toraji_2007_track.png"><img alt="Toraji 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Toraji_2007_track.png/150px-Toraji_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Toraji_2007_track.png/225px-Toraji_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Toraji_2007_track.png/300px-Toraji_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 4 – July 5</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 km/h (40 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  994 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>An area of disturbed weather formed in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> on July 2 and gradually consolidated over the next two days as it moved west-northwestward. A <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> was issued by the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> on the morning of July 4, and later that day the disturbance was upgraded straight to a tropical storm just south-east of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hainan_Island" title="Hainan Island">Hainan Island</a>. It made landfall on the island shortly after. China claimed that a tropical depression formed in the morning on July 2, made landfall in Hainan later that afternoon with maximum sustained winds of 15 m/s (55 km/h, 35 mph)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> and deepened to 988hPa<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> before making its second landfall.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> upgraded the tropical depression to Tropical Storm Toraji on the morning of July 5 while it was in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Tonkin" title="Gulf of Tonkin">Gulf of Tonkin</a>, after the centre of the storm had emerged back over water. The name <i>Toraji</i> was contributed by <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and refers to the broad bellflower (<i>platycodi radix</i>).</p>
<p>Toraji made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> around 1200 UTC later that evening, having not strengthened much while over the Gulf of Tonkin. The JMA never analysed the storm beyond 994 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> and minimal tropical storm strength. The JTWC issued its last advisory after landfall, and the JMA followed suit shortly after.</p>
<p>Throughout Guangxi Province, an estimated 1.11 million people were affected by Toraji.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> Heavy rains produced by the storm inundated an estimated 7,500 hectares of farmland and damaged 1,300 homes. The flooding forced about 147,000 people to evacuate to safer locations. Damages from the storm amounted to ¥73.6 million ($9.7 million USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several small fishing boats sank off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, the fate of the crews are unknown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW1_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW1-34">[33]</a></sup> Several other offshore incidents occurred, including a few collisions resulting in a minor oil spill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> Throughout northern areas of the country, an average of 155 mm (6.1 in) of rain fell, leading to flooding and landslides. At least 27 homes were damaged and 13 others were destroyed by the storm, leaving hundreds of millions of <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_dong" title="Vietnamese dong">Vietnamese dong</a> in losses. A power station at a military base was damaged during the storm, leaving roughly 40 million (VND; $2,240 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Man-yi_.28Bebeng.29">Typhoon Man-yi (Bebeng)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Typhoon Man-yi (Bebeng)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 super typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Man-Yi_12_july_2007_0505Z.jpg"><img alt="Man-Yi 12 july 2007 0505Z.jpg" data-file-height="7800" data-file-width="6000" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Man-Yi_12_july_2007_0505Z.jpg/150px-Man-Yi_12_july_2007_0505Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Man-Yi_12_july_2007_0505Z.jpg/225px-Man-Yi_12_july_2007_0505Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Man-Yi_12_july_2007_0505Z.jpg/300px-Man-Yi_12_july_2007_0505Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Man-yi_2007_track.png"><img alt="Man-yi 2007 track.png" data-file-height="869" data-file-width="1024" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Man-yi_2007_track.png/150px-Man-yi_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Man-yi_2007_track.png/225px-Man-yi_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Man-yi_2007_track.png/300px-Man-yi_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 9 – July 16</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>185 km/h (115 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  930 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> began to track an area of disturbed weather just north of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a> on July 4. The circulation centre and surrounding convection started to take shape, although the system was in a "marginal upper-level environment" with moderate vertical <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-04WABPWFAIR_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-04WABPWFAIR-38">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">Surface pressure</a> drops of less than 0.5 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mb</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>) were observed on July 6, as the system moved westward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-04WABPWFAIR_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-04WABPWFAIR-38">[37]</a></sup> Early on July 7, the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> (JMA) listed the system as a weak tropical depression. Hours later, the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> (JTWC) issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a>, as the system consolidated further with "deep convective banding" and improving upper-level conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>The JTWC issued its first warning on Tropical Depression 04W later that day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> and forecast a gradual intensification, as weak to moderate wind shear and weak poleward <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> balanced the effect of high ocean heat content.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> The JMA began issuing full tropical cyclone advisories on the tropical depression at the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> As the depression gained more organisation, it was upgraded to a tropical storm that night by the JTWC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> The JMA finally upgraded it to a tropical storm later that evening as the large system consolidated, naming it <i>Man-yi</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> The name "Man-yi" was contributed by Hong Kong, and is the Chinese name of a <a href="/wiki/Strait" title="Strait">strait</a> turned reservoir (the <a href="/wiki/High_Island_Reservoir" title="High Island Reservoir">High Island Reservoir</a>). Man-yi continued to organize and became a severe tropical storm on July 9, when downed electricity lines caused widespread power outages on <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> Tropical storm warnings and typhoon watches were put in place for most of <a href="/wiki/Yap_State" title="Yap State">Yap State</a> at some point during the storm. Strong waves from the typhoon capsized a ship 375 miles (604 km) to the northwest of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>, killing three and leaving six missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>The JTWC upgraded the storm to a typhoon on the afternoon of July 10, based on <a href="/wiki/Dvorak_technique" title="Dvorak technique">Dvorak technique</a> satellite intensity estimates of 65 knots (120 km/h) by both the JMA and the JTWC. Early the next day, the system entered the Philippine Area of Responsibility and was named "Bebeng" by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a>. At the same time, the JMA upgraded Man-yi to a typhoon.</p>
<p>Moving over warmer waters, Man-yi underwent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapid deepening</a> late on July 11 and early on July 12 as it churned towards <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okinawa" title="Okinawa">Okinawa</a> in Japan. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Military" title="United States Military">United States Military</a> upgraded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Condition_of_Readiness" title="Tropical Cyclone Condition of Readiness">Tropical Cyclone Condition of Readiness</a> (TCCOR) levels for <a href="/wiki/Kant%C5%8D_region" title="Kantō region">Kantō</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CFAY" title="CFAY">Yokosuka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sasebo,_Nagasaki" title="Sasebo, Nagasaki">Sasebo</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okinawa" title="Okinawa">Okinawa</a> on the afternoon of July 12 as Man-yi neared the islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Man-yi was upgraded twice to super-typhoon strength over the next day as it passed through the prefecture, with a 1-minute peak of 155 mph (249 km/h). The passage of Man-yi resulted in 37 injuries and widespread power outages in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okinawa" title="Okinawa">Okinawa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> The TCCOR level for Okinawa was downgraded to 1R (recovery) on July 13 while Kantō, Yokosuka and Sasebo's levels were all upgraded in anticipation of the typhoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Man-yi made brief landfall in <a href="/wiki/Kagoshima_Prefecture" title="Kagoshima Prefecture">Kagoshima Prefecture</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ky%C5%ABsh%C5%AB" title="Kyūshū">Kyūshū</a> early the next day before turning to the east and making brief landfalls in <a href="/wiki/K%C5%8Dchi_Prefecture" title="Kōchi Prefecture">Kōchi Prefecture</a> on <a href="/wiki/Shikoku" title="Shikoku">Shikoku</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Wakayama_Prefecture" title="Wakayama Prefecture">Wakayama Prefecture</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honsh%C5%AB" title="Honshū">Honshū</a>.</p>
<p>As it interacted with land and started to undergo <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extratropical_transition" title="Extratropical transition">extratropical transition</a>, the typhoon weakened and was downgraded to a tropical storm by the JTWC and a severe tropical storm by the JMA. It became extratropical on July 15 according to the JTWC and hence it issued its final advisory. The JMA issued its final advisory two days later.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Usagi">Typhoon Usagi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Typhoon Usagi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 super typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Usagi_01_aug_2007_0125Z.jpg"><img alt="Usagi 01 aug 2007 0125Z.jpg" data-file-height="8800" data-file-width="6800" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Usagi_01_aug_2007_0125Z.jpg/150px-Usagi_01_aug_2007_0125Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Usagi_01_aug_2007_0125Z.jpg/225px-Usagi_01_aug_2007_0125Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Usagi_01_aug_2007_0125Z.jpg/300px-Usagi_01_aug_2007_0125Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Usagi_2007_track.png"><img alt="Usagi 2007 track.png" data-file-height="701" data-file-width="1024" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Usagi_2007_track.png/150px-Usagi_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Usagi_2007_track.png/225px-Usagi_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Usagi_2007_track.png/300px-Usagi_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 27 – August 4</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>165 km/h (105 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  945 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On July 26, the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> identified an area of disturbed weather east of the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a>. This area moved westward and increased in organization, and the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> on the system on July 27.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> designated the system a tropical depression later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> The next day, the JMA began issuing advisories on the depression, and the JTWC followed suit, designating it Tropical Depression 05W.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>The system quickly strengthened as it approached the Mariana Islands, and the JTWC upgraded it to a tropical storm six hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> The JMA did so early on July 29, designating the system as Tropical Storm Usagi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> The name <i>Usagi</i> was contributed by Japan, and means "<i>rabbit</i>" in Japanese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-names_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-names-16">[15]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service</a> office in <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> issued <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">tropical storm warnings</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pagan_Island" title="Pagan Island">Pagan Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agrihan" title="Agrihan">Agrihan</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">Northern Marianas</a> shortly after the system was upgraded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Usagi passed between Pagan and Agrihan later on July 29,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> and began to quickly strengthen. The JTWC upgraded it to a typhoon later that day, citing <a href="/wiki/Dvorak_technique" title="Dvorak technique">Dvorak technique</a> numbers indicating an estimate of 65 <a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">knots</a> (120 km/h, 75 mph) and a developing <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> The system gradually turned toward the northwest, and the JMA upgraded it to a severe tropical storm early on July 30,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> and then to a typhoon on July 31 as it passed to the south of <a href="/wiki/Iwo_Jima" title="Iwo Jima">Iwo Jima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> Usagi moved northwest over warm waters, reaching peak intensity on August 1 before weakening due to cooling <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperatures</a> and increasing wind shear as it approached <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ky%C5%ABsh%C5%AB" title="Kyūshū">Kyūshū</a>. Usagi made landfall on August 2 near <a href="/wiki/Nobeoka,_Miyazaki" title="Nobeoka, Miyazaki">Nobeoka, Miyazaki</a> as a rapidly weakening typhoon, and it was downgraded to a severe tropical storm shortly after. The system continued weakening rapidly as it moved across Kyūshū and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honsh%C5%AB" title="Honshū">Honshū</a>, and the JMA downgraded it to a tropical storm later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>The JTWC downgraded the system to a tropical storm late on August 2 and issued its last advisory early on August 3 as it began to undergo <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical transition</a>. Usagi then made further landfalls on northern Honshū in <a href="/wiki/Aomori_Prefecture" title="Aomori Prefecture">Aomori Prefecture</a> before becoming fully extratropical on August 4, leading the JMA to stop advisories. Usagi was responsible for 18 injuries in Kyūshū.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_06W">Tropical Depression 06W</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression 06W">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_06W_04_aug_2007_0210Z.jpg"><img alt="TS 06W 04 aug 2007 0210Z.jpg" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="1800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/TS_06W_04_aug_2007_0210Z.jpg/150px-TS_06W_04_aug_2007_0210Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/TS_06W_04_aug_2007_0210Z.jpg/225px-TS_06W_04_aug_2007_0210Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/TS_06W_04_aug_2007_0210Z.jpg/300px-TS_06W_04_aug_2007_0210Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:6-W_2007_track.png"><img alt="6-W 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/6-W_2007_track.png/150px-6-W_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/6-W_2007_track.png/225px-6-W_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/6-W_2007_track.png/300px-6-W_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 2 – August 6</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>55 km/h (35 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  1000 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>An area of disturbed weather developed in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> on July 31. Despite strong <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> in the area, the system gradually increased in organization as it remained nearly stationary, and the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> on the system on August 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> The JTWC classified the system as Tropical Depression 06W shortly after,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> with the JMA designating it a tropical depression at the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> Despite strong <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> in the area, the system slowly intensified as it meandered along the coast of <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, and the JTWC upgraded it to a tropical storm early on August 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> However, later that day, the JTWC downgraded the storm back to a depression due to the loss of most of the convection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>At least 60 people died in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> due to extensive floods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> Total rainfall from 06W in Vietnam throughout the course of the storm was over 24 inches (610 mm). Total rainfall in Hainan during the passage of the tropical storm was 9.1 inches (230 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> In Thailand, the remnants of the storm lead to two casualties and about 272,757,962 Baht ($7.5 million US$) in damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Pabuk_.28Chedeng.29">Typhoon Pabuk (Chedeng)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Typhoon Pabuk (Chedeng)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pabuk_07_aug_2007_0107Z.jpg"><img alt="Pabuk 07 aug 2007 0107Z.jpg" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1600" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Pabuk_07_aug_2007_0107Z.jpg/150px-Pabuk_07_aug_2007_0107Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Pabuk_07_aug_2007_0107Z.jpg/225px-Pabuk_07_aug_2007_0107Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Pabuk_07_aug_2007_0107Z.jpg/300px-Pabuk_07_aug_2007_0107Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pabuk_2007_track.png"><img alt="Pabuk 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Pabuk_2007_track.png/150px-Pabuk_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Pabuk_2007_track.png/225px-Pabuk_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Pabuk_2007_track.png/300px-Pabuk_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 4 – August 10</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>120 km/h (75 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  975 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Pabuk_(2007)" title="Typhoon Pabuk (2007)">Typhoon Pabuk (2007)</a></div>
<p>A tropical disturbance developed southeast of <a href="/wiki/Chuuk_State" title="Chuuk State">Chuuk</a> early on July 31. The system moved west-northwestward over the next several days with little change in organization. On August 4, however, organized convection quickly began to redevelop, and the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> began monitoring it as a tropical depression. The system continued to strengthen, and the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> on the system early the next day, noting that its environment was "strongly favorable for development".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> designated the system Tropical Storm Pabuk shortly after.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> The name "<i>Pabuk</i>" was submitted by <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>, and refers to a large freshwater fish in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mekong_River" title="Mekong River">Mekong River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-names_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-names-16">[15]</a></sup> The JTWC designated the system Tropical Storm 07W at about the same time, and on August 5 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> named the system Chedeng. As Pabuk continued to move to the northwest, it gained some organisation as it slowly developed <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> It was upgraded by the JMA to a severe tropical storm on August 6. Moving westwards towards <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, an area of convection south of Pabuk separated and formed its own low-level circulation. Pabuk's upper-level outflow inhibited this new area of convection. Strengthening slightly, Pabuk was upgraded to a typhoon on the morning of August 7. The JTWC downgraded Pabuk to a tropical storm later that day, with the JMA downgrading Pabuk shortly before landfall. It made landfall in southern <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> around 1630 UTC according to Taiwan radar and crossed the southern tip of the <a href="/wiki/Hengchun" title="Hengchun">Hengchun</a> Peninsula in <a href="/wiki/Pingtung_County" title="Pingtung County">Pingtung County</a>. The JTWC re-upgraded Pabuk to a typhoon at its next advisory, however, citing a small eye at landfall,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> before downgrading it to a tropical storm again three hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>After passing over Taiwan, Pabuk took aim at Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a> and Macau's <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Meteorological_and_Geophysical_Bureau&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Meteorological and Geophysical Bureau (page does not exist)">Meteorological and Geophysical Bureau</a> both hoisted <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_tropical_cyclone_warning_signals" title="Hong Kong tropical cyclone warning signals">strong wind signal 3</a> on August 9 as the system passed to the south of Hong Kong. The JMA downgraded the storm to a tropical depression later that day and issued its final public advisory, with the JTWC following suit shortly after. The tropical depression then turned back to the east-northeast on August 10,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> forcing the HKO to re-issue signal 3. The HKO also warned that winds were expected to strengthen further locally, and that the Hong Kong Education Bureau had suspended all classes for the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> The HKO upgraded Pabuk to a tropical storm<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> and subsequently issued the gale or storm warning signal 8 at 2:30 pm <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Time" title="Hong Kong Time">HKT</a> (0630 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a>) later that day as Pabuk moved closer to the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> This was replaced by signal 3 later that night as Pabuk took another turn in direction and headed west inland into <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a>. Early next morning, Pabuk resumed a northeasterly track, edging once again closer to the Pearl River Delta<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> before it weakened further and HKO cancelled all signals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>At least 11 people were killed in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> by Pabuk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Wutip_.28Dodong.29">Tropical Storm Wutip (Dodong)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Wutip (Dodong)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wutip_09_aug_2007_0206Z.jpg"><img alt="Wutip 09 aug 2007 0206Z.jpg" data-file-height="1512" data-file-width="1512" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Wutip_09_aug_2007_0206Z.jpg/150px-Wutip_09_aug_2007_0206Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Wutip_09_aug_2007_0206Z.jpg/225px-Wutip_09_aug_2007_0206Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Wutip_09_aug_2007_0206Z.jpg/300px-Wutip_09_aug_2007_0206Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wutip_2007_track.png"><img alt="Wutip 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Wutip_2007_track.png/150px-Wutip_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Wutip_2007_track.png/225px-Wutip_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Wutip_2007_track.png/300px-Wutip_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 6 – August 9</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 km/h (40 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  990 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical disturbance developed to the south of the developing Tropical Storm Pabuk on August 5, and was first mentioned by the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> in its Significant Tropical Weather Outlook on August 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> designated it a tropical depression later that night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> By the next day, although still attached to Pabuk and being inhibited by <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">shearing</a> from an upper-level <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> <a href="/wiki/Anticyclone" title="Anticyclone">anticyclone</a> over Pabuk,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> the JTWC issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> As Pabuk moved away, the depression gradually strengthened, and the JMA designated it Tropical Storm Wutip early on August 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> The name <i>Wutip</i> was submitted by <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, and means <i><a href="/wiki/Butterfly" title="Butterfly">butterfly</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-names_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-names-16">[15]</a></sup> It struggled against land interaction, however, and did not strengthen considerably, remaining poorly organised. The storm quickly weakened, and the JMA issued its last advisory on Wutip early on August 9, downgrading it to a tropical depression. The JTWC issued its last advisory shortly after.</p>
<p>Upon being classified a tropical storm, ships within 450 km (280 mi) of the storm were advised to take precautions and those not within that range were urged to avoid it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tens of thousands of residents in the northern Philippines took shelter from the storm as there was a high likelihood over severe flooding due to already saturated grounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters1_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters1-90">[89]</a></sup> Schools throughout the area were canceled for several days due to the storm. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration</a> (PAGASA) placed <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Batanes,_Philippines&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Batanes, Philippines (page does not exist)">Batanes</a> under storm signal 2 while the <a href="/wiki/Babuyan_Islands" title="Babuyan Islands">Babuyan Islands</a> were under storm signal 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GMA1_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-GMA1-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taoyuan_City" title="Taoyuan City">Taoyuan County, Taiwan</a> (now Taoyuan City), a level three emergency response warning was put in place as Wutip approached the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> Fourteen flights in and out of Taiwan were canceled due to the approaching storm and all ferry service was canceled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Previously saturated by Typhoon Pabuk, the <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">outer bands</a> of Wutip produced torrential rains over <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>, Philippines, triggering numerous landslides and flash flooding. Two people were killed in a landslide in northern Luzon while another was electrocuted in knee-deep flooding in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manila,_Philippines" title="Manila, Philippines">Manila</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters1_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters1-90">[89]</a></sup> Widespread street flooding resulted in large traffic jams and numerous road closures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GMA1_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-GMA1-91">[90]</a></sup> Ten homes were destroyed and another 32 were damaged by Wutip. A total of six people were killed by the storm, three due to electrocution, and seven were injured due to a tornado. A total of 239,292 people were affected by the storm and damages amounted to <a href="/wiki/Philippine_peso" title="Philippine peso">PHP</a>16.8 million (US$349,000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NDCC1_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-NDCC1-94">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the flooding, the civil defense operations center in the Philippines deployed relief teams supplied with food to assist the affected regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters1_90-2"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters1-90">[89]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Sepat_.28Egay.29">Typhoon Sepat (Egay)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Typhoon Sepat (Egay)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5 super typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sepat_16_aug_2007_0225Z.jpg"><img alt="Sepat 16 aug 2007 0225Z.jpg" data-file-height="10801" data-file-width="8437" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Sepat_16_aug_2007_0225Z.jpg/150px-Sepat_16_aug_2007_0225Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Sepat_16_aug_2007_0225Z.jpg/225px-Sepat_16_aug_2007_0225Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Sepat_16_aug_2007_0225Z.jpg/300px-Sepat_16_aug_2007_0225Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sepat_2007_track.png"><img alt="Sepat 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Sepat_2007_track.png/150px-Sepat_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Sepat_2007_track.png/225px-Sepat_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Sepat_2007_track.png/300px-Sepat_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 12 – August 20</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>205 km/h (125 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  910 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Sepat_(2007)" title="Typhoon Sepat (2007)">Typhoon Sepat (2007)</a></div>
<p>An area of disturbed weather developed west of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">Northern Mariana Islands</a> on August 11. Early the next day, the JMA began issuing advisories on the depression,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> and the JTWC followed suit, designating it Tropical Depression 09W.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> Twelve hours later, the JTWC upgraded the tropical depression to a tropical storm<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> based on <a href="/wiki/Dvorak_technique" title="Dvorak technique">Dvorak technique</a> satellite intensity estimates and<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-09W_prog_2_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-09W_prog_2-98">[97]</a></sup> the storm exhibiting tightly-curved <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_convection" title="Atmospheric convection">convective</a> bands. An upper-level low helped to reduce <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> that had been affecting the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-09W_prog_2_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-09W_prog_2-98">[97]</a></sup> The JTWC also warned of the possibility of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">rapid intensification</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-09W_prog_2_98-2"><a href="#cite_note-09W_prog_2-98">[97]</a></sup> The JMA upgraded the depression to a tropical storm later that day<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> and named it Sepat, a name contributed by <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> referring to a freshwater fish species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-names_16-5"><a href="#cite_note-names-16">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>By early on August 13, Sepat had moved into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a>'s area of responsibility and attained the local name "Egay". The JMA upgraded Sepat to a severe tropical storm shortly after.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> Late that night, Sepat underwent rapid intensification as expected, and was upgraded by the JTWC to a super typhoon the next morning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-09W_prog_12_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-09W_prog_12-101">[100]</a></sup> Sepat slowed in forward speed and took a turn from a west-southwest motion to a more poleward one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-09W_prog_14_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-09W_prog_14-102">[101]</a></sup> Continuing to intensify,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-09W_prog_16_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-09W_prog_16-103">[102]</a></sup> Sepat reached a peak minimum central pressure of 910 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> on the morning of August 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> High <a href="/wiki/Ocean_heat_content" title="Ocean heat content">ocean heat content</a> and good <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equatorward</a> <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> allowed Sepat to maintain its intensity, but an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a> began later that night, resulting in weakening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-09W_prog_18_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-09W_prog_18-105">[104]</a></sup> It made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> in eastern <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> between <a href="/wiki/Taitung_City" title="Taitung City">Taitung</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hualien_City" title="Hualien City">Hualien</a> on the morning of August 18 local time at around 5 am (2100 UTC August 17)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> and weakened to a minimal typhoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> After crossing the island, Sepat held on to minimal typhoon intensity before weakening to a severe tropical storm that night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> It made a second landfall, in mainland China, about 24 hours after landfall on Taiwan and was downgraded to a tropical storm the next morning. It further weakened inland and the JMA issued its final advisory on the morning of August 20.</p>
<p>On August 15, monsoon rains brought by Typhoon Sepat flooded and paralyzed traffic in <a href="/wiki/Metro_Manila" title="Metro Manila">Metro Manila</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> Classes and services in government offices were suspended until August 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Fitow">Typhoon Fitow</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Typhoon Fitow">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fitow_06_sept_2007_0415Z.jpg"><img alt="Fitow 06 sept 2007 0415Z.jpg" data-file-height="7800" data-file-width="6000" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Fitow_06_sept_2007_0415Z.jpg/150px-Fitow_06_sept_2007_0415Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Fitow_06_sept_2007_0415Z.jpg/225px-Fitow_06_sept_2007_0415Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Fitow_06_sept_2007_0415Z.jpg/300px-Fitow_06_sept_2007_0415Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fitow_2007_track.png"><img alt="Fitow 2007 track.png" data-file-height="669" data-file-width="1024" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Fitow_2007_track.png/150px-Fitow_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Fitow_2007_track.png/225px-Fitow_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Fitow_2007_track.png/300px-Fitow_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 29 – September 8</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>130 km/h (80 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  965 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Fitow_(2007)" title="Typhoon Fitow (2007)">Typhoon Fitow (2007)</a></div>
<p>On August 28, an area of disturbed weather that had lingered east-northeast of <a href="/wiki/Saipan" title="Saipan">Saipan</a> became better organised. The <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> initiated warnings on Tropical Depression 10W the next morning,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> and the JMA initiated advisories on a tropical depression the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> Under favourable conditions, the system intensified quickly, becoming Tropical Storm Fitow by afternoon<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> and a severe tropical storm by the evening of August 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> The name <i>Fitow</i> was contributed by the <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</a>, and is <a href="/wiki/Yapese_language" title="Yapese language">Yapese</a> for a beautiful fragrant flower.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-names_16-6"><a href="#cite_note-names-16">[15]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">Rapid intensification</a> ensued,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> and Fitow became a typhoon early on August 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> Fitow made landfall near Tokyo, Japan late on September 6<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> as a minimal typhoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> The JMA downgraded Fitow to a severe tropical storm early on September 7,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> and a tropical storm later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> The cyclone degenerated into a remnant low on September 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Japan, seven people were killed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VancouverSun_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-VancouverSun-123">[122]</a></sup> and at least 50 were injured, as Fitow brought strong winds and heavy rain. Over 80,000 houses experienced a <a href="/wiki/Power_outage" title="Power outage">power outage</a>. Transport in and around Tokyo was also affected, with nearly 200 flights cancelled and many commuter trains suspended. In the <a href="/wiki/Western_Tokyo" title="Western Tokyo">Tama area</a> west of central Tokyo, flood warnings were issued for the <a href="/wiki/Tama_River" title="Tama River">Tama River</a>, and many homeless people who lived along its banks were swept away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Danas">Severe Tropical Storm Danas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Danas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Danas_09_sept_2007_2318Z.jpg"><img alt="Danas 09 sept 2007 2318Z.jpg" data-file-height="880" data-file-width="880" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Danas_09_sept_2007_2318Z.jpg/150px-Danas_09_sept_2007_2318Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Danas_09_sept_2007_2318Z.jpg/225px-Danas_09_sept_2007_2318Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Danas_09_sept_2007_2318Z.jpg/300px-Danas_09_sept_2007_2318Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Danas_2007_track.png"><img alt="Danas 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Danas_2007_track.png/150px-Danas_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Danas_2007_track.png/225px-Danas_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Danas_2007_track.png/300px-Danas_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 7 – September 11</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>100 km/h (65 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  990 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
