<p>A disturbed area of weather northwest of <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a> formed early on September 3 and tracked north then northwest, becoming more organised, and on September 6 was recognised as a full tropical depression by the JMA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> A TCFA was issued on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> The storm continued northwest-ward toward Japan, becoming Tropical Storm Danas early on September 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> The storm slowed its westward movement and headed north, and then northeast, becoming a severe tropical storm on September 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> By the 11th, cooler waters had weakened the storm down to a tropical storm<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> and the storm degenerated into a remnant low later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> The name <i>Danas</i> was submitted by the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and is defined in the Filipino language as "to go through an experience"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> High waves from Danas injured two people in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-132">[131]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Nari_.28Falcon.29">Typhoon Nari (Falcon)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Typhoon Nari (Falcon)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nari_15_sept_2007_0235Z.jpg"><img alt="Nari 15 sept 2007 0235Z.jpg" data-file-height="6800" data-file-width="5200" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Nari_15_sept_2007_0235Z.jpg/150px-Nari_15_sept_2007_0235Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Nari_15_sept_2007_0235Z.jpg/225px-Nari_15_sept_2007_0235Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Nari_15_sept_2007_0235Z.jpg/300px-Nari_15_sept_2007_0235Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nari_2007_track.png"><img alt="Nari 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Nari_2007_track.png/150px-Nari_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Nari_2007_track.png/225px-Nari_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Nari_2007_track.png/300px-Nari_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 11 – September 17</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>185 km/h (115 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  935 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Nari_(2007)" title="Typhoon Nari (2007)">Typhoon Nari (2007)</a></div>
<p>An area of disturbed weather developed northwest of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> on September 10 and moved northwestward, slowly increasing in organisation. The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> began monitoring the system as a tropical depression the next day. The depression continued to organise and strengthen, and the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> on it during the afternoon of September 12, and began issuing advisories on Tropical Depression 12W an hour later. The JMA followed suit early on September 13 and initiated advisories on the system; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> named the system Falcon shortly after. The depression continued to intensify, and the JMA upgraded it to Tropical Storm Nari later that morning. The storm then underwent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapid intensification</a> that afternoon and evening, strengthening from a tropical depression to a typhoon in just 18 hours. The JMA upgraded Nari to a severe tropical storm late that afternoon, and by late that evening, Nari was upgraded to a typhoon. Nari reached its peak on September 14, and began weakening soon afterwards. It turned extratropical right after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> in South Korea at tropical storm strength. At least 20 people have been killed or are missing due to the flooding caused by Nari. Rainfall totals reached a record 590 mm (23.2 in) in <a href="/wiki/Jeju_City" title="Jeju City">Jeju</a>, South Korea. The name <i>Nari</i> was submitted by South Korea, and means <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lily" title="Lily">lily</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-names_16-7"><a href="#cite_note-names-16">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Wipha_.28Goring.29">Typhoon Wipha (Goring)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Typhoon Wipha (Goring)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 super typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wipha_18_sept_2007_044Z_cropped.jpg"><img alt="Wipha 18 sept 2007 044Z cropped.jpg" data-file-height="6400" data-file-width="5600" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Wipha_18_sept_2007_044Z_cropped.jpg/150px-Wipha_18_sept_2007_044Z_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Wipha_18_sept_2007_044Z_cropped.jpg/225px-Wipha_18_sept_2007_044Z_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Wipha_18_sept_2007_044Z_cropped.jpg/300px-Wipha_18_sept_2007_044Z_cropped.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wipha_2007_track.png"><img alt="Wipha 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Wipha_2007_track.png/150px-Wipha_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Wipha_2007_track.png/225px-Wipha_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Wipha_2007_track.png/300px-Wipha_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 15 – September 20</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>185 km/h (115 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  925 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Wipha_(2007)" title="Typhoon Wipha (2007)">Typhoon Wipha (2007)</a></div>
<p>An area of disturbed weather formed southeast of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naha,_Okinawa" title="Naha, Okinawa">Naha, Okinawa</a> early on September 13. This area gradually became better organised, and a TCFA was issued late on September 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> The JMA upgraded the storm to a tropical depression on September 15,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> and the JTWC soon followed suit with Tropical Depression 13W.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> named the storm "Goring" later that day. On September 16, the storm had gained enough organisation to be designated as a tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> On September 17, the storm underwent rapid intensification and quickly strengthened into a typhoon. It continued to strengthen rapidly and was upgraded by the JTWC to a super typhoon early on September 18. In the early hours, local time, of September 19, Wipha slammed into <a href="/wiki/Fuding" title="Fuding">Fuding</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>–<a href="/wiki/Zhejiang" title="Zhejiang">Zhejiang</a> provincial border in China. However, before the storm made landfall it weakened slightly, becoming a Category 3-equivalent typhoon.</p>
<p>Wipha originally threatened to pass over Shanghai, which would have made it the most destructive Chinese typhoon in over a decade. However, it veered to the south, making a direct impact unlikely. Throughout the Shanghai and Fujian-Zhejiang area, nearly 2 million persons <a href="/wiki/Emergency_evacuation" title="Emergency evacuation">evacuated</a>, including 1.5 million in Zhejiang and 291 thousand from low-lying areas, due to the threat from Wipha. The <a href="/wiki/Xinhua_News_Agency" title="Xinhua News Agency">Xinhua News Agency</a> considered the evacuations to be the region's most extensive in over a half century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VancouverSun_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-VancouverSun-123">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>Boats, ferries, and ships were called back into port to take refuge in harbors. At both airports in Shanghai, at least twenty flights were canceled and fifty postponed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VancouverSun_123-2"><a href="#cite_note-VancouverSun-123">[122]</a></sup> The typhoon also caused <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> to reschedule four matches in the <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2007 FIFA Women's World Cup">Women's World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>Flooding was severe. In the area, at least 80 streets were flooded and brought water levels in several rivers and reservoirs to dangerous levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VancouverSun_123-3"><a href="#cite_note-VancouverSun-123">[122]</a></sup> In total, nine people were killed and damage was estimated at over $880 million (US$).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-138">[137]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_14W">Tropical Depression 14W</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression 14W">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TD_14W_21_sept_2007_0034Z.jpg"><img alt="TD 14W 21 sept 2007 0034Z.jpg" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="1800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/TD_14W_21_sept_2007_0034Z.jpg/150px-TD_14W_21_sept_2007_0034Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/TD_14W_21_sept_2007_0034Z.jpg/225px-TD_14W_21_sept_2007_0034Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/TD_14W_21_sept_2007_0034Z.jpg/300px-TD_14W_21_sept_2007_0034Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:14-W_2007_track.png"><img alt="14-W 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/14-W_2007_track.png/150px-14-W_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/14-W_2007_track.png/225px-14-W_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/14-W_2007_track.png/300px-14-W_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 20 – September 21</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>55 km/h (35 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  1000 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>An area of disturbed weather formed about 460 nmi (850 km) west of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> early on September 19. It was recognised as a minor tropical depression by the JMA later that day. On September 20, the JTWC initiated advisories on Tropical Depression 14W.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> Initially forecast to become a tropical storm, it was impacted by strong vertical wind shear and degenerated into a remnant low on September 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Francisco">Tropical Storm Francisco</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Francisco">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Francisco_24_sept_2007_0314Z.jpg"><img alt="Francisco 24 sept 2007 0314Z.jpg" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="1400" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Francisco_24_sept_2007_0314Z.jpg/150px-Francisco_24_sept_2007_0314Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Francisco_24_sept_2007_0314Z.jpg/225px-Francisco_24_sept_2007_0314Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Francisco_24_sept_2007_0314Z.jpg/300px-Francisco_24_sept_2007_0314Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Francisco_2007_track.png"><img alt="Francisco 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Francisco_2007_track.png/150px-Francisco_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Francisco_2007_track.png/225px-Francisco_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Francisco_2007_track.png/300px-Francisco_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 21 – September 25</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>75 km/h (45 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  990 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>An area of disturbed weather formed about 190 nmi (350 km) south-southeast of Hong Kong early on September 19. It was recognised as a minor tropical depression by the JMA on the 21st, and upgraded to a full depression on the 23rd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> The JTWC recognised Tropical Depression 15W at the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> Nine hours after being declared a full depression, the JMA and the JTWC upgraded it to Tropical Storm Francisco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> The storm traveled due west and over <a href="/wiki/Wenchang" title="Wenchang">Wenchang</a> on <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan Island</a> on September 24. Land interaction and moderate wind shear caused Francisco to weaken to a tropical depression as warnings were discontinued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> The name 'Francisco' was submitted by the United States and is a common <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_people" title="Chamorro people">Chamorro</a> man's name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> A ship, carrying eight people sank over the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> during the storm. Two of the people on the ship were rescued but the other six were listed as missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Lekima_.28Hanna.29">Severe Tropical Storm Lekima (Hanna)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Lekima (Hanna)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lekima_03_oct_2007_0306Z.jpg"><img alt="Lekima 03 oct 2007 0306Z.jpg" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Lekima_03_oct_2007_0306Z.jpg/150px-Lekima_03_oct_2007_0306Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Lekima_03_oct_2007_0306Z.jpg/225px-Lekima_03_oct_2007_0306Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Lekima_03_oct_2007_0306Z.jpg/300px-Lekima_03_oct_2007_0306Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lekima_2007_track.png"><img alt="Lekima 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Lekima_2007_track.png/150px-Lekima_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Lekima_2007_track.png/225px-Lekima_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Lekima_2007_track.png/300px-Lekima_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 28 – October 4</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>110 km/h (70 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  975 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical disturbance wave near the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> gradually developed. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> was first to upgrade it, declaring it Tropical Depression Hanna on September 27, and upgrading it to a tropical storm the next day. It made landfall in central <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a> early on September 29, and shortly thereafter the JMA declared the system Tropical Storm Lekima. It continued to strengthen and was upgraded to a severe tropical storm on September 30 (the JTWC upgraded it to a typhoon) and remained at such until landfall. It dissipated over land on October 5<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMABestTrackforstsLekima_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMABestTrackforstsLekima-150">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tropical Storm Lekima brought heavy rains to Luzon causing a landslide that killed eight people, including three children, in <a href="/wiki/Hingyon,_Ifugao" title="Hingyon, Ifugao">Ifugao province</a>, while another person was found dead in <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">Quezon City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HannaGMANews_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-HannaGMANews-151">[150]</a></sup> Torrential rains also caused landslides, flooding, infrastructure damage, and disruption of transportation service in other parts of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HannaGMANews_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-HannaGMANews-151">[150]</a></sup> Over 100,000 people were evacuated in southern China as the storm approached, and more than 20,000 fishing boats were recalled back to the <a href="/wiki/Harbor" title="Harbor">harbors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-138">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 3, Lekima made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> as a severe tropical storm. About 100,000 houses were destroyed and at least 42 people were reported dead or missing in Vietnam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Haiyan">Tropical Storm Haiyan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Haiyan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Storm_Haiyan_05_oct_2007_0205Z.jpg"><img alt="Tropical Storm Haiyan 05 oct 2007 0205Z.jpg" data-file-height="4600" data-file-width="3900" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Tropical_Storm_Haiyan_05_oct_2007_0205Z.jpg/150px-Tropical_Storm_Haiyan_05_oct_2007_0205Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Tropical_Storm_Haiyan_05_oct_2007_0205Z.jpg/225px-Tropical_Storm_Haiyan_05_oct_2007_0205Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Tropical_Storm_Haiyan_05_oct_2007_0205Z.jpg/300px-Tropical_Storm_Haiyan_05_oct_2007_0205Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haiyan_2007_track.png"><img alt="Haiyan 2007 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Haiyan_2007_track.png/150px-Haiyan_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Haiyan_2007_track.png/225px-Haiyan_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Haiyan_2007_track.png/300px-Haiyan_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 30 – October 7</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>75 km/h (45 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  994 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Haiyan_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Haiyan (2007)">Tropical Storm Haiyan (2007)</a></div>
<p>A tropical depression formed northeast of <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a> late on September 30. <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">JTWC</a> best track data analysed that the system developed into a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_cyclone" title="Subtropical cyclone">subtropical depression</a> on October 2 and transformed into a tropical depression at noon on October 3. In RSMC best track data, <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">JMA</a> analysed that Haiyan had already intensified into a tropical storm early on October 5, as well as the storm had already formed a cloud-filled <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a>. Early on October 6, JMA operationally upgraded the system to a tropical storm and named it <i>Haiyan</i>, but JMA’s post-analysis indicated that Haiyan started to weaken and soon become a tropical depression later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> On October 7, Haiyan dissipated, and the remnants were later absorbed by the new <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> transitioned from Podul. Originally not recognised by JTWC, Haiyan was added to the best track database and designated as <i>27W</i> in post-analysis.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Krosa_.28Ineng.29">Typhoon Krosa (Ineng)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Typhoon Krosa (Ineng)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 super typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Krosa_05_oct_2007_0215Z.jpg"><img alt="Krosa 05 oct 2007 0215Z.jpg" data-file-height="9400" data-file-width="7200" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Krosa_05_oct_2007_0215Z.jpg/150px-Krosa_05_oct_2007_0215Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Krosa_05_oct_2007_0215Z.jpg/225px-Krosa_05_oct_2007_0215Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Krosa_05_oct_2007_0215Z.jpg/300px-Krosa_05_oct_2007_0215Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Krosa_2007_track.png"><img alt="Krosa 2007 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Krosa_2007_track.png/150px-Krosa_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Krosa_2007_track.png/225px-Krosa_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Krosa_2007_track.png/300px-Krosa_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 1 – October 8</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>195 km/h (120 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  925 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In late September, a new system formed east of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. PAGASA declared it a tropical depression (Ineng) early on October 1, and the JMA and JTWC soon followed. It was upgraded to a tropical storm early on October 2, named Krosa. Rapid intensification took place on October 2 and it was upgraded to a typhoon by the JTWC by midday. As it intensified, it gained a wide, ragged eye and began to track to the west, becoming a typhoon by the JMA early on October 3. It continued to rapidly intensify that day before leveling off as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 4-equivalent</a> typhoon on October 4. Fluctuations in intensity soon followed as Krosa approached <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, as the JMA upgraded it to 105 knots (194 km/h) and the JTWC to a super typhoon early on October 5. It slowly weakened afterward before making landfall in northeastern <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> on October 6. At least 17 people were reported injured there, as the typhoon headed for China. An evacuation of 730,000 people from China's <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang" title="Zhejiang">Zhejiang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> provinces was ordered on the evening of October 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup> The extratropical remnants of Krosa crossed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Dateline" title="International Dateline">International Dateline</a> on October 12.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Podul">Severe Tropical Storm Podul</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Podul">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Podul_06_oct_2007_0009Z.jpg"><img alt="Podul 06 oct 2007 0009Z.jpg" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="640" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Podul_06_oct_2007_0009Z.jpg/150px-Podul_06_oct_2007_0009Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Podul_06_oct_2007_0009Z.jpg/225px-Podul_06_oct_2007_0009Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Podul_06_oct_2007_0009Z.jpg/300px-Podul_06_oct_2007_0009Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Podul_2007_track.png"><img alt="Podul 2007 track.png" data-file-height="781" data-file-width="1024" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Podul_2007_track.png/150px-Podul_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Podul_2007_track.png/225px-Podul_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Podul_2007_track.png/300px-Podul_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 3 – October 7</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>100 km/h (65 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  985 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On October 6, a tropical depression east of Japan was upgraded to Tropical Storm Podul while racing northeast. It was short-lived over the northwest Pacific and degenerated into a remnant low early on October 7. One person was killed due to the effects of Podul in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-132">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was upgraded to severe tropical storm status by JMA in post analysis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMA_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMA-155">[154]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Lingling">Tropical Storm Lingling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Lingling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lingling_12_oct_2007_2309Z.jpg"><img alt="Lingling 12 oct 2007 2309Z.jpg" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="480" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Lingling_12_oct_2007_2309Z.jpg/150px-Lingling_12_oct_2007_2309Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Lingling_12_oct_2007_2309Z.jpg/225px-Lingling_12_oct_2007_2309Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Lingling_12_oct_2007_2309Z.jpg/300px-Lingling_12_oct_2007_2309Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lingling_2007_track.png"><img alt="Lingling 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Lingling_2007_track.png/150px-Lingling_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Lingling_2007_track.png/225px-Lingling_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Lingling_2007_track.png/300px-Lingling_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 11 – October 15</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>85 km/h (50 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  994 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On October 9, a disturbance from the North Central Pacific crossed the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>, and became a tropical depression in the North Western Pacific, just east of the Date Line on October 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> It was upgraded to Tropical Storm Lingling by the JMA,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> and to Tropical Storm 18W by the JTWC, early on October 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> Lingling headed northeast, and gradually became weaker. On October 13, the JTWC issued its final advisory,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> and two days later the JMA did the same.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Kajiki">Typhoon Kajiki</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Typhoon Kajiki">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 super typhoon (SSHWS)</td>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kajiki_Oct_20_2007_0530Z.png"><img alt="Kajiki Oct 20 2007 0530Z.png" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1024" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Kajiki_Oct_20_2007_0530Z.png/150px-Kajiki_Oct_20_2007_0530Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Kajiki_Oct_20_2007_0530Z.png/225px-Kajiki_Oct_20_2007_0530Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Kajiki_Oct_20_2007_0530Z.png/300px-Kajiki_Oct_20_2007_0530Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kajiki_2007_track.png"><img alt="Kajiki 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Kajiki_2007_track.png/150px-Kajiki_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Kajiki_2007_track.png/225px-Kajiki_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Kajiki_2007_track.png/300px-Kajiki_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 19 – October 22</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>165 km/h (105 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  940 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>An area of disturbed weather formed in the open ocean early on October 17, and tracked north-east. The JMA and the JTWC declared this area a tropical depression very early on October 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup> Six hours later, it was upgraded to Tropical Storm Kajiki.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">Rapid intensification</a> continued; another six hours later, it was upgraded to a severe tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup> Kajiki became a typhoon early on October 20 as it rapidly intensified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> The storm reached peak intensity as it hit <a href="/wiki/Iwo_Jima" title="Iwo Jima">Iwo Jima</a> and then gradually began weakening. The storm dropped upwards of 233 mm (9.1 in) of rain on the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> The airport on Iwo Jima reported winds gusts up to 140 km/h (85 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Faxai_.28Juaning.29">Severe Tropical Storm Faxai (Juaning)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Faxai (Juaning)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faxai_27_oct_2007_0134Z.jpg"><img alt="Faxai 27 oct 2007 0134Z.jpg" data-file-height="3960" data-file-width="4096" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Faxai_27_oct_2007_0134Z.jpg/150px-Faxai_27_oct_2007_0134Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Faxai_27_oct_2007_0134Z.jpg/225px-Faxai_27_oct_2007_0134Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Faxai_27_oct_2007_0134Z.jpg/300px-Faxai_27_oct_2007_0134Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JMA_Faxai_2007_track.png"><img alt="JMA Faxai 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/JMA_Faxai_2007_track.png/150px-JMA_Faxai_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/JMA_Faxai_2007_track.png/225px-JMA_Faxai_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/JMA_Faxai_2007_track.png/300px-JMA_Faxai_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 25 – October 27</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>100 km/h (65 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  975 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Faxai_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Faxai (2007)">Tropical Storm Faxai (2007)</a></div>
<p>On October 25, an area of disturbed weather was classified as a tropical depression by the JMA;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup> early the next day the JMA named it Tropical Storm Faxai as it moved north-west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup> The JTWC picked the system up as a tropical depression early on the 26th,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> but declared it extratropical twelve hours later without strengthening it to a tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> declared the system Tropical Storm Juaning around the same time the JTWC picked it up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup> Later on October 26, the JTWC resumed advisories as a tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> The JMA declared Faxai a severe tropical storm as October 27 began;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup> the same day, the JTWC stopped issuing advisories once more due to Faxai having completed its extratropical transition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> The JMA also stopped issuing advisories on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>Faxai killed one person and injured three others in Japan. One home, two hectares of farmland, and 2 km (1.2 mi) of roads were damaged by the storm. At the height of the storm, 9,605 residences were without power. Heavy rains trigged seven mudslides throughout the country. One ship sank during the storm. Total damages from Faxai totaled to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JPY" title="JPY">¥</a>150 million ($1.5 million US$).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_132-2"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-132">[131]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Peipah_.28Kabayan.29">Typhoon Peipah (Kabayan)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Typhoon Peipah (Kabayan)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peipah_06_nov_2007_0124Z.jpg"><img alt="Peipah 06 nov 2007 0124Z.jpg" data-file-height="1360" data-file-width="1360" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Peipah_06_nov_2007_0124Z.jpg/150px-Peipah_06_nov_2007_0124Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Peipah_06_nov_2007_0124Z.jpg/225px-Peipah_06_nov_2007_0124Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Peipah_06_nov_2007_0124Z.jpg/300px-Peipah_06_nov_2007_0124Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pepiah_2007_track.png"><img alt="Pepiah 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Pepiah_2007_track.png/150px-Pepiah_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Pepiah_2007_track.png/225px-Pepiah_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Pepiah_2007_track.png/300px-Pepiah_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>November 3 – November 9</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>130 km/h (80 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  970 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>An area of disturbed weather developed east of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> on November 2. it was designated as Tropical Depression 21W &amp; Tropical Depression Kabayan by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> on November 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> It then went on to rapidly develop later that day and was upgraded to Tropical Storm Peipah by the JMA on November 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> Pepiah is a popular pet fish in <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-names_16-8"><a href="#cite_note-names-16">[15]</a></sup> Early on November 4 it was upgraded to a severe tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> Later that day, just before landfall in the northern Philippines, the JTWC upgraded it to a typhoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> Upon landfall in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palanan" title="Palanan">Palanan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabela_Province" title="Isabela Province">Isabela Province</a>, it pounded strong winds over Northern Luzon, thus unroofing houses, downing power lines and blocking many roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup> Once it emerged in the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Sea" title="Philippine Sea">Philippine Sea</a>, the JMA also upgraded it to a typhoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup> The strengthening trend was short-lived, though, as hindered <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> weakened the system on November 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup> It dissipated on November 9 before reaching <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Tapah">Tropical Storm Tapah</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Tapah">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tapah_12_nov_2007_0059Z.jpg"><img alt="Tapah 12 nov 2007 0059Z.jpg" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tapah_12_nov_2007_0059Z.jpg/150px-Tapah_12_nov_2007_0059Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tapah_12_nov_2007_0059Z.jpg/225px-Tapah_12_nov_2007_0059Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tapah_12_nov_2007_0059Z.jpg/300px-Tapah_12_nov_2007_0059Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tapah_2007_track.png"><img alt="Tapah 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Tapah_2007_track.png/150px-Tapah_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Tapah_2007_track.png/225px-Tapah_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Tapah_2007_track.png/300px-Tapah_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>November 11 – November 13</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 km/h (40 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  996 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Early on November 8, the JTWC reported that an area of convection had persisted about 910 km, (565 miles), to the east of Guam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STWA_08110706z_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-STWA_08110706z-186">[185]</a></sup> Quickscat data had revealed that there was weak troughing at the surface but no closed low level circulation center existed. Lying under the edge of an upper level ridge the disturbance was in an area of moderate amount vertical windshear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STWA_08110706z_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-STWA_08110706z-186">[185]</a></sup> Over the next couple of days an anticyclone helped to develop the disturbance so that the JMA declared it a Tropical Depression on November 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMA_ATCR_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMA_ATCR-187">[186]</a></sup> Later that morning a TCFA, was issued by the JTWC later that morning as deep convection was now organizing into a partially exposed low level circulation center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup> Later that day the JTWC designated the depression, as 22W whilst it was located 530 km, (330 miles), to the southwest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iwo_To" title="Iwo To">Iwo To</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PROG_1_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-PROG_1-189">[188]</a></sup> The Depression at this stage was beginning to turn towards the north with deep convection consolidating since the TCFA was released, and was strongest along the northern edge of the system which was enhanced by poleward outflow into the midlatitude <a href="/wiki/Westerlies" title="Westerlies">westerlies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PROG_1_189-1"><a href="#cite_note-PROG_1-189">[188]</a></sup> Early on November 12, the depression was upgraded to a Tropical Storm by both the JMA and the JTWC with the name Tapah being assigned whilst located to the southeast of <a href="/wiki/Iwo_Jima" title="Iwo Jima">Iwo Jima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMA_ATCR_187-1"><a href="#cite_note-JMA_ATCR-187">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWC_BT_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC_BT-190">[189]</a></sup> Both 1-minute and 10-minute peak windspeeds of 65 km/h, (40 mph), were reached as the JMA and the JTWC upgraded the depression to Tapah.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMA_ATCR_187-2"><a href="#cite_note-JMA_ATCR-187">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWC_BT_190-1"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC_BT-190">[189]</a></sup> It remained at this intensity until later that day when both the JMA and the JTWC downgraded it to a Tropical Depression, and issued their final advisories whilst it was going through an extratropical transition before it dissipated early on November 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMA_ATCR_187-3"><a href="#cite_note-JMA_ATCR-187">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWC_BT_190-2"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC_BT-190">[189]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Hagibis_.28Lando.29">Typhoon Hagibis (Lando)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Typhoon Hagibis (Lando)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 typhoon (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hagibis_23_nov_2007_0213Z.jpg"><img alt="Hagibis 23 nov 2007 0213Z.jpg" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Hagibis_23_nov_2007_0213Z.jpg/150px-Hagibis_23_nov_2007_0213Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Hagibis_23_nov_2007_0213Z.jpg/225px-Hagibis_23_nov_2007_0213Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Hagibis_23_nov_2007_0213Z.jpg/300px-Hagibis_23_nov_2007_0213Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hagibis_2007_track.png"><img alt="Hagibis 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Hagibis_2007_track.png/150px-Hagibis_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Hagibis_2007_track.png/225px-Hagibis_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Hagibis_2007_track.png/300px-Hagibis_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>November 18 – November 28</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>130 km/h (80 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  970 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On November 18 The <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> issued a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TCFA" title="TCFA">TCFA</a> on a Tropical Disturbance located east of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. Later that day the disturbance was upgraded to a Tropical Depression 24W by the JTWC. PAGASA also declared it Tropical Depression Lando early on November 19, and also upgraded it to a tropical storm soon after. The JTWC also upgraded it to a tropical storm that day. Early on November 21, the storm strengthened into a severe tropical storm. Later that afternoon, the JTWC upgraded Hagibis to typhoon status, and the JMA followed late that evening. The storm then wobbled off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> beginning on November 22 where it gradually weakened. By November 24, due to its interaction with <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_typhoon_season#Typhoon_Mitag_.28Mina.29" title="2007 Pacific typhoon season">Typhoon Mitag</a>, the storm turned back eastward in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> towards the Philippines once again. The JTWC issued its final advisory on November 27, although it was maintained by the JMA as it made landfall once again over the Philippines. It weakened to a depression east of the Philippines on November 28 and the JMA issued its final advisory.</p>
<p>Hagibis caused the deaths of nine people, all in the <a href="/wiki/Visayas" title="Visayas">Visayas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">Mindanao</a> island groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup></p>
<p>The name <i>Hagibis</i> was submitted by the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and is defined in the Filipino dictionary as "rapid".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mitag_23_nov_0146Z.jpg"><img alt="Mitag 23 nov 0146Z.jpg" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Mitag_23_nov_0146Z.jpg/150px-Mitag_23_nov_0146Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Mitag_23_nov_0146Z.jpg/225px-Mitag_23_nov_0146Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Mitag_23_nov_0146Z.jpg/300px-Mitag_23_nov_0146Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mitag_2007_track.png"><img alt="Mitag 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Mitag_2007_track.png/150px-Mitag_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Mitag_2007_track.png/225px-Mitag_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Mitag_2007_track.png/300px-Mitag_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>

<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>November 20 – November 27</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>150 km/h (90 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  955 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Mitag_(2007)" title="Typhoon Mitag (2007)">Typhoon Mitag (2007)</a></div>
<p>On November 20 an area of disturbed weather east of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> strengthened and was classified as Tropical Storm Mitag by the JMA. The JTWC followed suit not long afterwards. The storm strengthened significantly early on November 21 and became a severe tropical storm. Later that day, the JTWC upgraded Mitag to a typhoon, and the JMA also upgraded it late that evening.</p>
<p>Philippine officials started the evacuation of about 200,000 people on November 23, mostly from the <a href="/wiki/Bicol_Region" title="Bicol Region">Bicol Region</a> as the Mitag approaches the coast. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_the_Philippines" title="Province of the Philippines">province</a> of Albay has declared a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_calamity" title="State of calamity">state of calamity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>As Mitag remained stationary in the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Sea" title="Philippine Sea">Philippine Sea</a> for a day as a Category 2-equivalent typhoon, it changed its course and instead of hitting <a href="/wiki/Catanduanes" title="Catanduanes">Catanduanes</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bicol_Region" title="Bicol Region">Bicol Region</a>, it will make a landfall at the <a href="/wiki/Aurora_(province)" title="Aurora (province)">Aurora</a>–<a href="/wiki/Isabela_(province)" title="Isabela (province)">Isabela</a> area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup> Nonetheless, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> announced that there is still a possibility of the typhoon to once again change its course. The storm turned northwest towards northern <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a> and made landfall late on November 25. It tracked across the island and was downgraded to a severe tropical storm before emerging back over water on November 26. It turned back to the east before reaching <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, and became extratropical on November 27.</p>
<p>Ten persons were reportedly killed due to the effects of Typhoon Mina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup> The remnants of Mitag contributed to heavy rains in Okinawa which damaged 3 km (1.9 mi) of roads and triggered one landslide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_132-3"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-132">[131]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_25W">Tropical Depression 25W</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression 25W">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TD_25W_MODIS_Terra_27_nov_0231Z.jpg"><img alt="TD 25W MODIS Terra 27 nov 0231Z.jpg" data-file-height="842" data-file-width="944" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/TD_25W_MODIS_Terra_27_nov_0231Z.jpg/150px-TD_25W_MODIS_Terra_27_nov_0231Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/TD_25W_MODIS_Terra_27_nov_0231Z.jpg/225px-TD_25W_MODIS_Terra_27_nov_0231Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/TD_25W_MODIS_Terra_27_nov_0231Z.jpg/300px-TD_25W_MODIS_Terra_27_nov_0231Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:25-W_2007_track.png"><img alt="25-W 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/25-W_2007_track.png/150px-25-W_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/25-W_2007_track.png/225px-25-W_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/25-W_2007_track.png/300px-25-W_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>November 25 – November 27</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 km/h (30 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  1004 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On November 24 an area of disturbed area formed about 400 nmi (740 km) south east of Guam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABPW10_24-11-07_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABPW10_24-11-07-197">[196]</a></sup> During the following day the JTWC issued a TCFA on the developing system whilst the JMA designated it as a minor tropical depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWJP25_Warning_25-11-07_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWJP25_Warning_25-11-07-198">[197]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCFA_25-11-07_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCFA_25-11-07-199">[198]</a></sup> On November 26 the JTWC designated the depression as Tropical depression 25W<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWC_Advisorys_25-11-07_09z_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC_Advisorys_25-11-07_09z-200">[199]</a></sup> Over the next couple of days it tracked towards the north west maintaining its peak wind speeds of 25 kts (45 km/h 30 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWC_Best_track_27W_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC_Best_track_27W-201">[200]</a></sup> The depression then started its extra tropical transition on November 27 as it interacted with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baroclinic_zone" title="Baroclinic zone">Baroclinic zone</a>, the JTWC then issued its final warning on 25W.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWC_Advisorys_27-11-07_15z_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC_Advisorys_27-11-07_15z-202">[201]</a></sup> This was because the depression would succumb to the increasing vertical sheer and decreasing sea surface temperatures as it completed its extra tropical transition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWC_Advisory_27-11-07_21z_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC_Advisory_27-11-07_21z-203">[202]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_26W">Tropical Depression 26W</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression 26W">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (JMA)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TD_26W_MODIS_IR_Terra_28_nov_1233Z.jpg"><img alt="TD 26W MODIS IR Terra 28 nov 1233Z.jpg" data-file-height="735" data-file-width="814" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/TD_26W_MODIS_IR_Terra_28_nov_1233Z.jpg/150px-TD_26W_MODIS_IR_Terra_28_nov_1233Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/TD_26W_MODIS_IR_Terra_28_nov_1233Z.jpg/225px-TD_26W_MODIS_IR_Terra_28_nov_1233Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/TD_26W_MODIS_IR_Terra_28_nov_1233Z.jpg/300px-TD_26W_MODIS_IR_Terra_28_nov_1233Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:26-W_2007_track.png"><img alt="26-W 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/26-W_2007_track.png/150px-26-W_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/26-W_2007_track.png/225px-26-W_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/26-W_2007_track.png/300px-26-W_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>November 28 – November 29</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 km/h (30 mph) <small>(10-min)</small>  1000 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Possibly from the remnants of 25W, an area of disturbed weather formed south-east of <a href="/wiki/Yap" title="Yap">Yap</a> on November 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABPW10_26-11-07_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABPW10_26-11-07-204">[203]</a></sup> The next day the JTWC issued a TCFA on the developing system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCFA_27-11-07_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCFA_27-11-07-205">[204]</a></sup> On November 28, the JMA declared it as a minor tropical depression, whilst later that day the JTWC followed suit and designated it as a tropical depression, with the JTWC assigning the number 26W to the depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMA_Advisory_28-11-07_12z_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMA_Advisory_28-11-07_12z-206">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWC_Advisory_28-11-07_15z_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC_Advisory_28-11-07_15z-207">[206]</a></sup> However the Tropical depression quickly became extratropical later that day with the JTWC issuing their final advisory on the storm later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWC_Advisory_28-11-07_21z_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC_Advisory_28-11-07_21z-208">[207]</a></sup> However the JMA continued to monitor the Depression until it dissipated the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMA_Advisory_29-11-07_06z_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMA_Advisory_29-11-07_06z-209">[208]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Storm names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Within the North-western Pacific Ocean, both the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> (JMA) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration</a> assign names to tropical cyclones that develop in the Western Pacific, which can result in a tropical cyclone having two names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Padgett_Dec_99_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_Dec_99-210">[209]</a></sup> The Japan Meteorological Agency's RSMC Tokyo — Typhoon Center assigns international names to tropical cyclones on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a>'s Typhoon Committee, should they be judged to have 10-minute sustained windspeeds of 65 km/h, (40 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TC_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-TC-211">[210]</a></sup> While the Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration assigns names to tropical cyclones which move into or form as a tropical depression in their area of responsibility located between 135°E and 115°E and between 5°N-25°N even if the cyclone has had an international name assigned to it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Padgett_Dec_99_210-1"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_Dec_99-210">[209]</a></sup> The names of significant tropical cyclones are retired, by both <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Philippine_typhoon_names" title="List of retired Philippine typhoon names">PAGASA</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_typhoon_names_(JMA)" title="List of retired Pacific typhoon names (JMA)">Typhoon Committee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TC_211-1"><a href="#cite_note-TC-211">[210]</a></sup> Should the list of names for the Philippine region be exhausted then names will be taken from an auxiliary list of which the first ten are published each season. Unused names are marked in <font color="#666666">gray</font>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_names">International names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: International names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lists_of_tropical_cyclone_names" title="Lists of tropical cyclone names">Lists of tropical cyclone names</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">Tropical cyclone naming</a></div>
<p>During the season 23 named tropical cyclones developed in the Western Pacific and were named by the Japan Meteorological Agency, when it was determined that they had become tropical storms. These names were contributed to a list of a 140 names submitted by the fourteen members nations and territories of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESCAP/WMO_Typhoon_Committee" title="ESCAP/WMO Typhoon Committee">ESCAP/WMO Typhoon Committee</a>. The name <i>Peipah</i> was used for the first time as it was replaced from <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Vamei" title="Tropical Storm Vamei">Vamei</a>.</p>

<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration</a> uses its own naming scheme for tropical cyclones in their area of responsibility. PAGASA assigns names to tropical depressions that form within their area of responsibility and any tropical cyclone that might move into their area of responsibility. Should the list of names for a given year prove to be insufficient, names are taken from an auxiliary list, the first 10 of which are published each year before the season starts. The names not retired from this list will be used again in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2011 Pacific typhoon season">2011 season</a>. This is the same list used in the <a href="/wiki/2003_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2003 Pacific typhoon season">2003 season</a>, except for the names <i>Bebeng</i>, <i>Hanna</i>, <i>Lando</i>, <i>Mina</i>, <i>Nonoy</i>, <i>Pedring</i>, <i>Ramon</i>, and <i>Sendong</i>, which replaces <i>Batibot</i>, <i>Harurot</i>, <i>Lakay</i>, <i>Manang</i>, <i>Niña</i>, <i>Pogi</i>, <i>Roskas</i>, and <i>Sikat</i>. The names Hanna, Lando and Mina were used for the first time this year; Bebeng was previously used in the <a href="/wiki/1999_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="1999 Pacific typhoon season">1999 season</a>. Names that were not assigned are marked in <font color="#666666">gray</font>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAGASAnames_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-PAGASAnames-212">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAGASA07uses_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-PAGASA07uses-213">[212]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Season effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This is a table of the storms in 2007 and their landfall(s), if any. Damage and deaths include totals while the storm was extratropical or a wave or low. The information below is mainly from the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a>. Names in parenthesis are those assigned by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a>.</p>
